## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This is a nonlinear harmonic oscillator problem where acceleration (dv_dt) is determined by restoring forces (dependent on position x), damping forces (dependent on velocity v), and possibly time-dependent driving forces. The nonlinearity can appear in the restoring force, damping, or both.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + linear damping)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x**2 * v (nonlinear damping)
- Driven harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (periodic driving)
- Driven Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven nonlinear oscillator)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (c1 + c2 * x**2) (position-dependent stiffness)
- Nonlinear damping with cubic velocity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (Rayleigh dissipation)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * cos(c1 * t) + c2 * v (time-modulated stiffness)
- Coulomb + viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * tanh(c3 * v) (mixed damping)
- General driven van der Pol: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (c2 + c3 * x**2) + c4 * cos(c5 * t) (full nonlinear driven-damped system)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium — use odd polynomial in x
- Position-dependent damping (x²·v term) indicates amplitude-dependent energy exchange — characteristic of self-excited oscillations like van der Pol
- Periodic driving forces appear as sin(c·t) or cos(c·t) terms added to autonomous dynamics
- If acceleration has no explicit time dependence, the system is autonomous and phase-plane analysis applies — try formulas without t
- Negative linear damping combined with positive nonlinear damping (c1·v + c2·v³ with opposite signs) indicates limit cycle behavior
- Sinusoidal restoring force sin(c·x) suggests rotational/pendulum dynamics rather than translational oscillation
- Parametric excitation manifests as multiplicative coupling between x and periodic functions of t (e.g., x·cos(c·t))
- Even-power terms in x (like x²) break oscillation symmetry and indicate asymmetric potential wells
